Drilled Shaft Load Test Report 
Test Shaft No. 2 
Tunnel Influent Pump Station and Headworks Facility 
Kailua Regional Wastewater Treatment Plant (RWWTP) 
Kailua, Oahu, Hawaii 
Dear Mr. Placencia: 
As requested, Geolabs, Inc. conducted a static compressive load test on a 
dedicated drilled shaft, designated as Test Shaft No. 2 (TS-2), for the Kailua RWWTP 
Tunnel Influent Pump Station and Headworks Facility project on July 12, 2016. This 
letter report presents the results of our field observations and the test data obtained 
during the drilled shaft load test. 
The compressive load test was conducted on a 30-inch diameter drilled shaft 
(designated as Test Shaft No. 2), and the approximate location of the test shaft is 
shown on the Test Shaft Location Plan, Plate 1. The ground elevation during the test 
shaft installation was estimated at about +11.5 feet Mean Sea Level (MSL). The test 
shaft was excavated to a tip elevation of about -64.6 feet MSL using a Watson 3100 drill 
rig equipped with a 30-inch diameter auger. After augering to near the tip elevation, 
approximately 61.2 feet of 30-inch diameter temporary steel casing was installed using 
a vibratory hammer followed by removal of the spoils from within the hole. 
Reinforcing steel and concrete was placed for the test shaft using a concrete pump 
discharging via a tremie pipe on June 29, 2016.  
A concrete form was used to bring the concrete level to approximately 3.2 feet 
above the existing grade to provide a platform for the load testing apparatus. During the 
test shaft installation, a Geotechnical Quality Control Specialist from our office 
maintained a record of our field observations, which is presented on Plates 2.1 through 
2.4. 
The test shaft was instrumented with 10 vibrating wire embedment strain gages 
(Model No. VCE-4200) manufactured by Geokon. The embedment strain gages were 
installed at intervals of about 8 feet along the load test shaft, with the first level at about

A multiplexer was used to connect the 10 embedment strain gages to a Geokon 
Micro-10 datalogger, which recorded the strains in the embedment strain gages during 
the compressive load test. During installation of the test shaft, Strain Gage Nos. SG-3, 
SG-5 and SG-6 appear to have been damaged and resulted in erroneous readings. 
Additionally, SG-1 was installed above the ground surface. Therefore, the results from 
these strain gages have been excluded from our analysis. 
The test shaft was loaded in general accordance with ASTM D1143/1143M 
Procedure A – Quick Test procedure. Test Shaft No. 2 (TS-2) was loaded to a test load 
of 240 kips in approximately 6-kip load increments. Each load increment was held for at 
least 8 minutes, at which point, the rate of the test shaft head movement was stable. In 
addition, the maximum test load was maintained for at least 1 hour to evaluate the 
effects of creep. Subsequently, the test load was unloaded in five decrements, and each 
unload decrement was held for about 4 minutes.  
It should be noted that due to the use of a larger diameter load test shaft of 
30 inches for the design drilled shaft diameter of 24 inches, we increased the maximum 
test load by 25% to account for the larger diameter of the load test shaft by 25% 
(30”/24”). Therefore, we increased the maximum test load from 200% of the design load 
to 250% of the design load for the 30-inch diameter load test shaft. Because the axial 
drilled shaft capacity was derived primarily from skin friction and the axial capacity is 
directly proportional to the perimeter of the drilled shaft, an increase in the maximum 
test load equivalent to the percent increase in the diameter. 
Healy Tibbitts Builders, Inc. 
Page 3 
W.O. 7320-30 (Test Shaft No. 2) 
July 22, 2016 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
After unloading, the test shaft was re-loaded to the previous maximum load of 
240 kips in approximately 48-kip load increments, held for at least 4 minutes. From 
200 kips, the test shaft was loaded to a maximum test load of 300 kips (250% of the 
design load) in approximately 15-kip load increments. These load increments were held 
for at least 15 minutes, at which point, the rate of the test shaft head movement was 
stable. Subsequently, the test load was unloaded in five decrements, and each unload 
decrement was held for about 4 minutes. 
Two dial gages supported on two reference beams installed on opposite sides of 
the test shaft and a survey level set at the center of the shaft were used to measure the 
shaft head displacement. The load test readings and the load-displacement curve are 
presented on Plates 3 and 4, respectively. The compressive load test results are 
summarized as follows. 
STATIC COMPRESSIVE LOAD TEST SUMMARY 
Shaft No. 
Test Shaft No. 2 
Shaft Length from Top of Shaft 
79.3 feet 
Maximum Test Load 
300 kips 
Total Displacement 
0.127 inches 
Rebound
0.037 inches
Net Displacement 
0.090 inches 
Based on the measured displacements of the compressive load test, the 30-inch 
diameter test shaft did not fail at the maximum test load of 300 kips. Strain changes 
from the four functioning embedment strain gages were recorded using a Micro-10 
datalogger during the compressive load test. Based on tests conducted the day after the 
load test, the unconfined compressive strength (f’c) of the test shaft concrete was 
reported at 6,240 psi. Using the ACI formula (Ec = 57,000 √f’c), the elastic modulus of 
the shaft concrete was estimated at 4,503,000 psi or 4,503 ksi. Using a shaft stiffness 
(AE) of 3,183,000 kips, the interpreted load transfer is presented graphically on Plate 5. 
In addition, the mobilized net side shear versus displacement curves based on the 
available strain gage data and estimated shaft stiffness are presented on Plate 6.  
A printout of the strain gage readings is presented in the Appendix. It should be 
noted that calibration records for the load cell and dial gages used in the load test have 
been submitted previously under separate cover prior to conducting the load test.

After concrete was pumped to top of casing, top 
of concrete was cleaned off and overflowed to 
expose good concrete. Vibratory hammer was 
then used to pull casing up approximately 16 feet 
above grade and was again filled to top of casing 
with concrete using gravity feed from the 
concrete pump truck boom. Casing was then 
removed and concrete level dropped to 
approximately 3 feet below the ground surface. 
Build-up casing (3 feet long) was then installed at 
ground surface and was leveled off. Pump truck 
was then attached to secondary tremie (20 feet 
long) installed with the rebar cage to fill up build-
up casing. However, concrete seeped out under 
build-up casing and instead had to be topped off 
using gravity feed methods.
